--- LESSON 4: the "outsourcing buyer discloses more" pattern now has a cleaner signal: it's not US-vs-China or captive-vs-not in the abstract — it's whether the SPECIFIC buyer builds the component in-house (Waymo Honeycomb, Figure, Apptronik, Agility = dead ends) vs buys merchant (Zoox→Hesai, Hyundai MobED→SOS Lab, Chinese humanoid OEMs→a deep tier-2/3 bench, Tesla Optimus→Hota candidate). China A-share disclosure of humanoid suppliers is real and dense, but the China robotics-supplier trade has ALREADY been discovered by domestic investors — most named names are already re-rated 100%+; the yield is in the SECOND-ORDER/less-famous names on those same BOM lists (Zhucheng, Xiangxin, Siling, Jiangsu Leili, Fenglong) that haven't been individually re-rated yet, not the headline names (Green Harmonic, Zhongda Leader). Next fire: run a cheap PRICE pre-gate pass (2-source) on the 8 UNKNOWN-price China names logged above before any deeper diligence. W-track remains genuinely hard — one dedicated fire found the right thematic fit (Xsens Humanoid mocap) but the equity is dead; the real supplier bench (Leopard Imaging and similar camera/depth-module integrators) is private. ---

--- LESSON 8: a capture-rate check that finds a NAMED COMPETITOR holding the buyer's own "preferred partner" award (Dingzhi Tech vs Moons') is now a repeatable pattern for killing crowded-field leads fast — check for the buyer's own PR "excellent/preferred supplier" awards before deep-diving a 1-of-N candidate. --- LESSON 7: the routine's "move toward a decision" discipline cuts both ways — this fire's two long-standing trigger checks (Hota's 6th PO-check, Jiangsu Leili's FY2025-report reveal) BOTH resolved negatively, taking WATCH count from 9 to 7. This is a feature, not a bug, of the idea-yield mandate (§17): fewer, higher-conviction names beat a padded list carrying names whose own binding-gate trigger just failed. The Orbbec-upstream vector is now CLOSED (one real supplier found, SmartSens, but immaterial to its revenue; the higher-value chip tier is in-house at Orbbec) and the Robbyant-ecosystem vector is CLOSED for now (all-private, one forward-listing to watch: Leju). Customs/bill-of-lading as a non-anchored METHOD underperformed for these specific buyer targets (Figure/Tesla/Waymo/Unitree/AgiBot) — public BoL/customs databases don't resolve component-level inflows to captive/obscured-intermediary assemblers; it did surface one already-run name (Sanhua) via secondary press, not primary trade data. 2026-07-10 | HSAI (Hesai Group) | MAJOR CORRECTION, not a new candidate — 8x market-cap error found and fixed (Opus, independently verified by orchestrator against a primary SEC 6-K) | Every prior fire (40/44/46/48) computed "true mkt cap" as POST-split ordinary-share count (1,257.1M) × ADS price ($16.40) ≈ $20.6B. This double-counts the Jul 10 2026 corporate action, which was an 8-for-1 ordinary-share subdivision PAIRED WITH a matching 1:1→1:8 ADS-ratio change, explicitly designed to be "economically neutral" (Hesai's own 6-K language, via TipRanks summary) — so the ADS price should NOT divide by 8. Price evidence confirms it: pre-split ADS ~$17-18 (Jun 30), post-split ADS $16.40 (Jul 9-10) — flat, not divided by ~8. CORRECT mkt cap = ADS-equivalent count (157.14M, unchanged) × $16.40 ≈ $2.58B — confirmed independently against MarketBeat ($2.30B) and CNN ($2.60B), the very aggregators the KB had repeatedly dismissed as wrong for this ticker. On FY25 revenue ~$433M this is ~6x sales, not ~40x. REVERSES the Fire 46/48 "asymmetry-decayed, fully priced" downgrade — HSAI reconfirmed strong #1, stays WATCH not BUY only due to the still-unresolved D.C.
